B|CATEGORY 11: SUPPLEMENTS & NUTRACEUTICALS
B|Comprehensive Treatment Research — OCD (Treatment-Resistant Focus)
N|25 research queries executed, narrowed from broad systematic reviews to compound-specific trial data
B|
B|A. AMINO ACIDS & DIRECT PRECURSORS
B|
B|🔬 NAC — N-Acetylcysteine
N|Mechanism: Glutamate modulator + antioxidant. Treatment-naïve OCD patients show significantly elevated glutamatergic activity; NAC normalizes this. Also replenishes glutathione — the brain's primary antioxidant defense system.
N|Evidence Level: Multiple RCTs — mixed but meaningful
B|Clinical Data:
N|Meta-analysis of 6 RCTs (195 patients): significant Y-BOCS improvement, but only within the 5–8 week window specifically
N|Benefit disappears under 5 weeks and beyond 12 weeks — timing is everything
N|One 16-week trial in treatment-resistant OCD showed no significant OCD score difference vs placebo, BUT showed significant anxiety reduction (p=0.02) — still clinically useful
N|Best performance as augmentation alongside SSRIs, not standalone
N|Dosage: 2,400–3,000 mg/day — split doses. Start at 600mg, ramp up over 2 weeksSide Effects: Abdominal pain (60% of users at full dose), nausea. Take with food.Sourcing: Widely available OTC, reputable brands include Jarrow, Thorne, Pure EncapsulationsCritical Note: Give it the full 6–8 week window before judging. Most people quit too early.
B|
B|🔬 Inositol (Myoinositol)
N|Mechanism: Second-messenger modulator acting intracellularly — unlike most psychiatric drugs that work at the receptor surface, inositol works inside the cell by regulating the phosphatidylinositol signaling cycle. It upregulates striatal dopamine D2 receptor density and reverses serotonin receptor desensitization. This is why it can work when SSRIs fail — entirely different mechanism.
N|Evidence Level: Placebo-controlled trial confirmed
B|Clinical Data:
N|Placebo-controlled study: 18g/day produced significant Y-BOCS improvement, effects emerging at 4 weeks
N|Comparable efficacy to SSRIs in some patients as monotherapy
N|Critical caveat: Adding inositol to SSRIs showed no additional benefit — works best either as standalone or when SSRIs have already failed
N|Dosage: Build to 18g/day — start at 2g, increase by 2g every 3–4 days. Split into 3 doses. Powder form only practical at this dose (capsules are impractical at 18g)Side Effects: GI — nausea, bloating, flatulence, diarrhea. Diminishes after 2–3 weeks. Take with food.Sourcing: Bulk powder (NOW Foods, Jarrow). 18g/day means you need bulk, not capsules.Cost: Very affordable even at therapeutic doses — approximately $30–40/month
B|
B|🔬 5-HTP (5-Hydroxytryptophan)
N|Mechanism: The most direct serotonin precursor available over the counter. Crosses the blood-brain barrier without a carrier molecule. Unlike L-tryptophan, not diverted into protein synthesis or niacin conversion — goes straight to serotonin. Stimulates cellular serotonin output directly.
N|Evidence Level: RCT data — strong
B|Clinical Data:
N|Double-blind multi-center study: 5-HTP as effective as fluvoxamine (Luvox) as standalone
N|Combination trial: 5-HTP + fluoxetine proved significantly more effective than fluoxetine alone at reducing OCD symptoms
N|Antidepressant effects may be equivalent to fluoxetine, with effects appearing in as little as two weeks
B|Dosage Protocol:
N|Week 1–2: 50mg at night
N|Week 3–4: 100mg at night
N|Week 5+: Up to 200mg/day (split if needed)
N|Research has used up to 800mg in depression trials — 200mg is considered the OCD-specific ceiling for safe self-administration
N|Take with: 25–50mg B6, 200–500mg Vitamin C, 10mg Magnesium (cofactors for conversion)
N|⚠️ Critical Interaction Warning: Combining with SSRIs carries serotonin syndrome risk. If currently on an SSRI, this combination requires careful monitoring. Do not combine without medical oversight or a very gradual, cautious titration.Sourcing: Griffonia simplicifolia extract — Source Naturals, NOW Foods, Doctor's Best
B|
B|🔬 L-Theanine
N|Mechanism: Increases GABA, serotonin, and dopamine. Enhances alpha brain wave activity (calm alertness without sedation). Modulates glutamate at NMDA receptors. Works synergistically with SSRIs without the serotonin syndrome risk.
N|Evidence Level: RCT confirmed — remarkable results
B|Clinical Data:
N|10-week RCT (50 participants): 200mg/day L-theanine combined with fluvoxamine produced 30–50% greater improvement in obsession scores
N|92% of the L-theanine group achieved complete response vs 36% of placebo group — a 2.5x difference. This is one of the most striking OCD supplement results in the literature.
N|Separate study confirmed significantly greater obsession subscale improvement
N|Dosage: 200–400mg/day. Can take as single dose or split AM/PM. Higher doses (400mg) studied for schizophrenia augmentation with antipsychotics.Side Effects: Essentially none. Minimal GI in some cases. One of the cleanest safety profiles of any neuropsychiatric supplement.Synergy: Particularly potent when combined with green tea's EGCG — L-theanine + EGCG work synergistically on anxiety and stress responseSourcing: Suntheanine brand (patented L-isomer form, highest purity). Available through many reputable brands.
B|
B|🔬 Glycine
N|Mechanism: NMDA receptor co-agonist — occupies the glycine binding site on NMDA receptors, modulating glutamate activity. High-dose glycine increases synaptic glycine availability, normalizing NMDA function in OCD-relevant circuits.
N|Evidence Level: Preliminary — case reports and small trials
B|Clinical Data:
N|Case reports and small open-label studies showed reduction in OCD symptoms at very high doses
N|NMDA hypofunction in OCD circuits is a legitimate target — glycine addresses this directly
N|Less studied than sarcosine for this purpose but mechanistically sound
N|Dosage: High doses required: 60g/day has been used in case reports (extremely high — GI issues common). More practical doses of 15–30g/day have shown effect. Start very low, ramp slowly.Side Effects: Nausea and GI distress at high doses. Sedation possible.Note: Glycine is abundant in collagen — collagen supplementation also raises glycine levels with better tolerability at lower doses
B|
B|🔬 Sarcosine (N-Methylglycine)
N|Mechanism: Glycine transporter-1 (GlyT-1) inhibitor — blocks reuptake of glycine at synapses, increasing extracellular glycine and enhancing NMDA receptor function. Produces less NMDAR desensitization than glycine itself, resulting in stronger, more sustained effects.
N|Evidence Level: Studied primarily in schizophrenia; OCD evidence limited but mechanistically well-supported
B|Clinical Data:
N|Clinical dose of 2g/day studied — well tolerated
N|Schizophrenia data robust for negative and cognitive symptoms via the same NMDA mechanism implicated in OCD
N|Logical OCD target given glutamate hypothesis
N|Dosage: 2g/day — practical, available as powderSide Effects: Generally well-tolerated. Mild GI in some.Sourcing: Grey market / research chemical suppliers, some supplement companies in Taiwan carry it. Available online.
B|
B|B. VITAMINS — DEFICIENCY-LINKED MECHANISMS
B|
B|🔬 Vitamin D3 (with K2)
N|Mechanism: Vitamin D deficiency reduces tryptophan hydroxylase synthesis → less serotonin production. Deficiency also removes neuroprotection (normally inhibits nitric oxide synthase) and dysregulates dopamine. Gut microbiota effects on serotonin synthesis also mediated through vitamin D. A biological cascade of downstream OCD-relevant effects.
N|Evidence Level: Observational correlation strong; supplementation trials promising
B|Clinical Data:
N|48.5% of OCD patients show vitamin D deficiency vs 20% of controls
N|Moderately negative correlation between serum vitamin D and Y-BOCS scores across multiple symptom dimensions
N|Supplementation study in young people: significant OCD symptom improvement
N|Children with OCD and low D3: 87.5% comorbid ADHD vs 52.6% in sufficient-D group
N|The Move: Test your serum 25(OH)D level before supplementing. Target: 60–80 ng/mL (most OCD patients are below 30)Dosage: If deficient: 5,000–10,000 IU D3 daily with K2 (100–200mcg MK-7 form) to direct calcium properly. Take with largest fat-containing meal.Monitoring: Retest at 3 months. Don't guess — test.Sourcing: Thorne D3/K2 drops, NOW Foods, any reputable D3+K2 combination
B|
B|🔬 Methylcobalamin (B12) + Methylfolate (L-5-MTHF)
N|Mechanism: OCD patients show significantly lower B12 and higher homocysteine than controls. The one-carbon metabolism pathway regulated by B12 and folate directly affects homocysteine levels — elevated homocysteine correlates with OCD severity. Additionally, the MTHFR gene mutation (present in ~40% of population) impairs conversion of regular folic acid to active methylfolate — these individuals cannot use standard folic acid supplements.
N|Evidence Level: RCT for B12+folate augmentation; observational for deficiency correlation; active clinical trial for methylfolate (NCT06218030)
B|Clinical Data:
N|OCD patients on SSRIs + B12/folate: statistically significant Y-BOCS improvement vs SSRIs alone
N|B12 deficiency partially mediates OCD-sleep disturbance relationship
N|Active trial investigating L-methylfolate specifically as adjunct for treatment-resistant OCD
B|The Protocol:
N|Test: serum B12, homocysteine, MTHFR gene variant (23andMe gives this data)
N|If MTHFR mutation present: use methylfolate, NOT folic acid — folic acid may actually block methylfolate receptors in MTHFR variants
N|B12 form: Methylcobalamin or hydroxocobalamin — not cyanocobalamin (synthetic, less bioavailable)
N|Dosage: Methylcobalamin 1,000–2,000mcg sublingual daily; Methylfolate 400–1,000mcg daily (start low, some MTHFR variants react poorly to high initial doses — "start low, go slow")
N|Sourcing: Thorne, Pure Encapsulations, Seeking Health (specifically formulates for MTHFR)
B|
B|🔬 Pyridoxine / P5P (Vitamin B6)
N|Mechanism: Critical cofactor for serotonin and dopamine synthesis — without adequate B6, your body cannot efficiently convert 5-HTP to serotonin or L-DOPA to dopamine. Also essential for GABA synthesis.
N|Evidence Level: Mechanistic/indirect; essential cofactor for other supplements on this list
N|Note: If taking 5-HTP, this is not optional — it's a required cofactor. Use P5P form (pyridoxal-5-phosphate), the active form. Regular B6 must be converted to P5P — some people convert poorly.Dosage: 25–50mg P5P daily. Do not exceed 100mg long-term without monitoring — high B6 can cause peripheral neuropathySourcing: Thorne P5P, Jarrow P5P
B|
B|🔬 Niacinamide (B3)
N|Mechanism: Niacinamide has anxiolytic properties via benzodiazepine receptor binding at high doses. Also supports NAD+ synthesis, which feeds mitochondrial function in neurons. Orthomolecular psychiatry has used high-dose niacinamide for psychiatric conditions since the 1950s.
N|Evidence Level: Theoretical/mechanistic for OCD specifically; anxiety evidence moderate
N|Dosage: 500–1,500mg/day. Niacinamide (not niacin — avoids flushing). Some orthomolecular protocols use 3g+/day under supervision.Caution: Liver enzyme monitoring recommended at high doses
B|
B|C. MINERALS
B|
B|🔬 Zinc
N|Mechanism: Inhibits excessive NMDA receptor activation — the same glutamate pathway implicated in OCD. Participates in 300+ enzymatic reactions. Directly influences neurotransmitter regulation and antioxidant defense.
N|Evidence Level: Deficiency confirmed in OCD populations; augmentation with SSRIs showing benefit
B|Clinical Data:
N|OCD patients show consistently lower serum zinc vs healthy controls, with negative correlation to symptom severity (especially in women)
N|2020 systematic review: zinc supplementation as adjunct to SSRIs led to greater symptom reduction than SSRIs alone in treatment-resistant cases
N|Dosage: Test first. If deficient: 25–30mg elemental zinc daily (zinc picolinate or bisglycinate forms — highest absorption). Take with food, away from copper supplements.Critical Interaction: Long-term zinc supplementation depletes copper — supplement 1–2mg copper per 25–30mg zinc, or use zinc+copper formulas.Sourcing: Thorne Zinc Picolinate, NOW Foods zinc bisglycinate
B|
B|🔬 Magnesium
N|Mechanism: Regulates neurotransmitter release broadly. Natural NMDA receptor antagonist (blocks the channel at rest). Calming effect on the nervous system. Magnesium deficiency is epidemic in Western populations — poor diet, soil depletion, stress depletion.
N|Evidence Level: Deficiency documented in OCD; supplementation evidence indirect
N|Clinical Data: OCD populations show lower serum magnesium vs controls. Magnesium regulates the same NMDA pathway targeted by memantine and ketamine — just more gently.
N|Dosage: 300–600mg elemental magnesium daily. Form matters enormously:
N|Magnesium L-threonate (Magtein) — crosses blood-brain barrier most effectively, cognitive benefits
N|Magnesium glycinate — high absorption, gentle on gut, calming
N|Magnesium malate — energy-supporting, good for daytime use
N|Avoid: Magnesium oxide — poor absorption, mostly used as laxative
N|Take: Magnesium glycinate at night (promotes sleep), Magtein morning/afternoon (cognitive)Sourcing: Magtein by Jarrow, Pure Encapsulations Magnesium Glycinate
B|
B|D. ANTIOXIDANTS & NEUROPROTECTIVES
B|
B|🔬 Curcumin (Enhanced Bioavailability Forms ONLY)
N|Mechanism: Serotonin upregulation via 5-HT1A receptor activation; dopamine modulation; anti-inflammatory via NF-κB inhibition; antioxidant. Animal models show significant OCD-like behavior reduction.
N|Evidence Level: Animal models strong; human data limited but positive; standard curcumin is essentially useless — bioavailability under 1%
B|The Bioavailability Problem & Solutions:
N|Standard curcumin powder: <1% bioavailable. Waste of money.
N|Piperine (BioPerine) + curcumin: Increases bioavailability up to 2,000% — the most studied combination. Use 2g curcumin + 20mg piperine. ⚠️ Piperine also inhibits CYP enzymes — can increase blood levels of other drugs significantly (including SSRIs). Monitor closely if on medications.
N|Phospholipid complex (Meriva, Phytosome): 29x bioavailability increase over standard. Gentler on drugs than piperine.
N|Theracurmin: Nanocolloidal dispersion, highly bioavailable, no piperine interaction
N|Liposomal curcumin: Encapsulates in lipid vesicles, lymphatic absorption
N|Longvida (solid lipid nanoparticle): Designed specifically for brain delivery
N|Recommended Form for OCD: Theracurmin or Longvida — brain-targeted delivery without the drug interaction risk of piperineDosage: Equivalent to 400–800mg curcuminoids daily in enhanced formSourcing: NOW Foods CurcuBrain (Longvida), Doctor's Best Theracurmin
B|
B|🔬 EGCG (Epigallocatechin Gallate) — Green Tea Extract
N|Mechanism: GABA-A receptor modulation (anxiolytic), HPA axis regulation, BDNF upregulation, anti-neuroinflammatory, neuroprotective. Synergizes powerfully with L-theanine — the two compounds co-occur naturally in green tea and enhance each other's effects.
N|Evidence Level: Small human trials; animal models strong
B|Clinical Data:
N|Reduced stress and improved mood in young adult trials
N|Combined L-theanine + EGCG: enhanced calming without sedation, buffered stress-induced heart rate elevation
N|Psychiatric patients: improved HAM-A (anxiety), HAM-D (depression), PANSS (psychotic symptoms) scores
N|Dosage: 400–800mg EGCG daily (standardized extract). High-dose, prolonged use (months) needed for psychiatric benefit.⚠️ Caution: High-dose EGCG on empty stomach can cause nausea; liver stress at very high doses (>800mg/day) — take with foodSynergy Note: Take L-theanine and EGCG together — they potentiate each other
B|
B|🔬 Sulforaphane (Broccoli Sprout Extract)
N|Mechanism: Activates Nrf2 — the master antioxidant regulatory pathway. Triggers glutathione production, reduces neuroinflammation, neuroprotective. 82% bioavailability (extraordinarily high for a plant compound — compare to curcumin's <1%). Broccoli sprouts contain 30x more glucoraphanin than mature broccoli.
N|Evidence Level: Autism data (same neuroinflammatory mechanisms as OCD); mechanistically strong for OCD neuroinflammation
N|Clinical Data: Autism trial showed decreased oxidative stress, improved neurotransmitters, positive hormonal changes — all relevant to OCD neuroinflammationDosage: 30–60mg sulforaphane daily (from extract) or grow/buy fresh broccoli sprouts (1/2 cup fresh sprouts)Important: Myrosinase enzyme needed to convert glucoraphanin to sulforaphane — either buy activated extract (check label) or add mustard seed powder to raw sproutsSourcing: Avmacol, Thorne Crucera-SGS, Jarrow BroccoMax
B|
B|E. ESSENTIAL FATTY ACIDS
B|
B|🔬 Omega-3 (EPA/DHA Fish Oil)
N|Mechanism: Anti-inflammatory, neuronal membrane fluidity, serotonin and dopamine receptor function modulation
N|Evidence Level: Weak for OCD specifically; moderate for general anxiety
B|Clinical Data:
N|Single OCD-specific trial (n=11): EPA added to SSRIs showed no benefit over placebo for OCD symptoms — very small trial, not definitive
N|Meta-analysis of 19 anxiety trials: significant anxiety reduction at doses >2,000mg/day
N|20% anxiety reduction in healthy adults at 12 weeks
N|The Honest Assessment: Weak direct OCD evidence. Valuable as anti-inflammatory baseline support, especially combined with other interventions. Don't lead with this.Dosage: 2,000–3,000mg combined EPA+DHA daily if using. EPA-dominant formulas for mood/anxiety (EPA:DHA ratio of 2:1 or higher)Sourcing: Nordic Naturals, Carlson Labs, Thorne — third-party tested for mercury
B|
B|F. HERBAL & BOTANICAL COMPOUNDS
B|
B|🔬 Valerian Root
N|Mechanism: GABA-A receptor activity — similar mechanism to benzodiazepines but without significant addiction risk at therapeutic doses. Anxiolytic.
N|Evidence Level: Single placebo-controlled RCT
B|Clinical Data:
N|RCT (n=31, 8 weeks): 765mg/day valerian extract produced significant OCD symptom improvement (p<0.0001)
N|Rapid onset — effects measured at days 28, 42, and 56
N|Lower libido impairment than pharmacological alternatives — clinically significant for quality of life
N|Dosage: 450–900mg standardized extract (0.8% valerenic acid) daily. Best taken 1–2 hours before bed.Side Effects: Drowsiness, occasional vivid dreams, paradoxical stimulation in small subsetCaution: Don't combine with benzodiazepines or alcoholSourcing: Nature's Way, Herb Pharm (high quality liquid extract), Gaia Herbs
B|
B|🔬 Borage (Borago officinalis) Extract
N|Mechanism: Not fully elucidated — contains GLA (gamma-linolenic acid), anti-inflammatory; rosmarinic acid, anxiolytic
N|Evidence Level: Single placebo-controlled RCT
B|Clinical Data:
N|Double-blind trial (n=24): significant improvement in OCD and anxiety symptoms at weeks 4 and 6 vs placebo
N|Side effects: mild gas, bloating, indigestion
N|Dosage: Study dose not published in accessible form — typically 1,000–2,000mg borage seed oil for GLA content⚠️ Warning: Some borage products contain pyrrolizidine alkaloids (PAs), which are hepatotoxic. Use only PA-free certified borage products.Sourcing: Limited — ensure PA-free certification on label
B|
B|🔬 Milk Thistle (Silymarin)
N|Mechanism: Silymarin's OCD mechanism unclear — antioxidant, anti-inflammatory, hepatoprotective. May affect serotonin systems.
N|Evidence Level: One head-to-head RCT vs fluoxetine
B|Clinical Data:
N|RCT (n=35, 8 weeks): 600mg/day silymarin vs fluoxetine — no significant difference in OCD symptom reduction. Comparable efficacy starting week 5.
N|Side effects similar to fluoxetine: nausea, sexual dysfunction
N|The Significance: Not because milk thistle is impressive — but because a plant compound matched an SSRI in a controlled trial. Worth considering if SSRI side effects are intolerable.Dosage: 420–600mg silymarin daily (standardized to 70–80% silymarins), split 3x dailySourcing: Thorne Siliphos (phospholipid form for absorption), Jarrow Milk Thistle
B|
B|🔬 Ashwagandha (KSM-66 or Sensoril)
N|Mechanism: HPA axis modulator — normalizes cortisol dysregulation (both elevated and depleted). Withanolides reduce neuroinflammation, support GABA activity. Adaptogenic — builds long-term stress resilience rather than acute sedation.
N|Evidence Level: Robust for anxiety/stress; indirect for OCD
B|Clinical Data:
N|33–38% reduction in perceived stress scores vs 26% placebo
N|44% stress reduction in another trial vs 5.5% placebo
N|Meta-analysis of 12 trials: significant serum cortisol reduction
N|28% cortisol reduction with improved sleep and cognitive function within 8–12 weeks
N|Dosage: KSM-66 extract: 300–600mg daily. Sensoril: 125–250mg daily (more concentrated). Take with meals.Note: Results build over 8–12 weeks — not an acute interventionSynergy: Works well combined with L-theanine (nervine) and melatonin (circadian support)Sourcing: KSM-66 by Jarrow, Ixoreal brand KSM-66, Sensoril by Natreon
B|
B|🔬 Passionflower (Passiflora incarnata)
N|Mechanism: GABAergic — increases GABA activity, promotes relaxation via CNS inhibition. More acute/immediate than ashwagandha. Contains chrysin, which may have mild benzodiazepine receptor activity.
N|Evidence Level: Anxiety evidence moderate; OCD specific limited
N|Dosage: 250–500mg standardized extract daily. Can be combined with ashwagandha for complementary coverage (nervine + adaptogen).Sourcing: Herb Pharm, Gaia Herbs, Nature's Answer
B|
B|🔬 St. John's Wort (Hypericum perforatum)
B|⚠️ Flagged — Mixed Evidence + Significant Drug Interactions
N|Mechanism: Weak SSRI + dopamine/norepinephrine reuptake inhibition
N|Evidence for OCD: Two small randomized trials with mixed results — one showed improvement over 12 weeks, another showed no difference vs placebo. Cannot be recommended with confidence for OCD specifically.
N|Critical Drug Interaction: Do not combine with SSRIs — serotonin syndrome risk. Also induces CYP3A4 enzyme, reducing blood levels of many medications including some antidepressants, making them less effective.
N|Verdict: If not on SSRIs and want a trial — possible. If on any antidepressant — avoid.
B|
B|🔬 Kava (Piper methysticum)
N|Mechanism: Kavalactones enhance GABA-A receptor activity (different binding site than benzodiazepines — potentially less addictive). Also influence dopamine and norepinephrine.
N|Evidence Level: Moderate for general/situational anxiety; NO direct OCD evidence found
B|Clinical Data:
N|Meta-analysis: significant anxiety reduction vs placebo
N|GAD: 120–240mg kavalactones significantly reduced anxiety scores (effect size 0.63–0.80)
N|Long-term GAD use: mild, non-significant benefit in 16-week trial — loses steam
N|Dosage: 70–250mg kavalactones daily. Use traditional water-based preparations or reputable extracts — not acetone/ethanol extracts (linked to liver toxicity).⚠️ Liver Safety: Documented hepatotoxicity with certain preparations — liver enzyme monitoring recommended for regular use. Avoid alcohol. Use noble kava varieties only.Sourcing: Kalm with Kava (traditional preparation), Gaia Herbs (standardized)
B|
B|G. CELLULAR ENERGY & CIRCADIAN BIOLOGY
B|
B|🔬 NAD+/NMN/Nicotinamide Riboside
N|Mechanism: NAD+ is essential for mitochondrial energy production and neurotransmitter synthesis (including serotonin and dopamine). Low NAD+ triggers NLRP3 inflammasome → inflammatory cytokines linked to depression and anxiety. Restoring NAD+ activates SIRT1, inhibiting neuroinflammation. Also normalizes oxytocin production (relevant to social anxiety dimension of OCD).
N|Evidence Level: Small human study + animal models
B|Clinical Data:
N|Small study: reduction in OCD symptom severity observed after NAD+ treatment
N|Autism mouse model: nicotinamide riboside restored oxytocin levels, corrected anxiety-like behavior and social deficits
N|IV NAD+ used clinically for addiction and psychiatric conditions
B|Dosage:
N|NMN: 500–1,000mg/day oral (sublingual for better absorption)
N|NR (Nicotinamide Riboside): 300–1,000mg/day
N|Combine with methylation support (TMG/betaine, 500–1,000mg) to prevent methyl group depletion
N|IV NAD+: Available at many wellness clinics — 500–1,000mg IV infusion. More direct cellular delivery. Grey market option: some clinics offer without requiring specific diagnosis.
N|Sourcing: Tru Niagen (NR, clinically studied brand), ProHealth NMN, Elysium Basis
B|
B|🔬 Melatonin + Circadian Interventions
N|Mechanism: OCD populations show later melatonin release than controls — many have Delayed Sleep Phase Disorder. Circadian dysregulation appears to maintain OCD symptoms. Melatonin correction is a genuine disease-modifying approach for this subset, not just sleep support.
N|Evidence Level: Case series + RCT for light therapy (circadian intervention)
B|Clinical Data:
N|Case series (7 OCD patients with circadian disruption): agomelatine (melatonin MT1/MT2 receptor agonist) reduced OCD symptoms 46–90% — dramatic results
N|Three patients without sleep disruption: zero response. This tells us circadian correction works specifically for the circadian-dysregulated subtype
N|Light therapy RCT: active light protocol (morning light + evening light reduction) > sham; 49-minute shift toward earlier sleep timing; largest improvement in intrusive thoughts
N|The Diagnostic Question: Do you have delayed sleep? Night owl tendencies? Difficulty sleeping before 1–2 AM? If yes, this category may be crucial.
B|The Protocol:
N|Melatonin 0.5–1mg (LOW dose — high doses suppress natural production) 5 hours before target bedtime
N|Morning bright light therapy: 10,000 lux lamp for 20–30 minutes immediately upon waking
N|Blue light blocking glasses after sunset
N|Consider agomelatine (prescription in many countries, available through online pharmacies) — melatonin receptor agonist with antidepressant properties
B|
B|H. ANTI-INFLAMMATORY COMPOUNDS
B|
B|🔬 PEA — Palmitoylethanolamide
N|Mechanism: Endogenous fatty acid amide — activates PPAR-α receptors, reducing glial activation, neuroinflammation, and mast cell markers. Modulates endocannabinoid tone (without THC effects). Increases GABA and dopamine turnover in the amygdala. Reduces TNF-α and IL-1β — the same inflammatory cytokines elevated in OCD brain imaging studies.
N|Evidence Level: Preclinical + early human data; explicitly suggested as adjunct for pediatric OCD and PANDAS tic disorders
B|Clinical Data:
N|MDD trial: 600mg twice daily with citalopram outperformed placebo on both depression and anxiety
N|Autism case series: 600–700mg/day improved behavior, sociability, irritability
N|Obesity model: improved anxiety-like behavior, increased GABA levels in amygdala, attenuated HPA axis overactivation
N|Explicitly suggested for PANDAS/OCD overlap — anti-neuroinflammatory with excellent safety profile
N|Dosage: 600–1,200mg/day. Some protocols use up to 1,800mg/day. Split 2–3x daily with food.Forms: Standard PEA or ultramicronized PEA (um-PEA) — ultramicronized has superior absorptionSafety: Exceptionally clean safety profile. No serious adverse events in trials.Sourcing: Levagen+ (ultramicronized, most studied form), PeaPlex
B|
B|🔬 Lithium Orotate (Low-Dose Supplement)
N|Mechanism: Inhibits GSK-3β (overactive in OCD), reduces oxidative stress and neuroinflammation via WNT/β-catenin pathway. Neuroprotective at low doses. Very different profile from prescription lithium carbonate.
N|Evidence Level: Theoretical/mechanistic for OCD; anxiety data from low-dose supplementation
B|Clinical Data:
N|Prescription lithium augmentation studies exist — but HIGH-dose lithium can actually worsen OCD (increases glutamate transmission). This is compound-specific.
N|Low-dose lithium orotate (~10mg elemental lithium): self-reported mood and anxiety improvement in surveys; clinical trial in bipolar depression: >50% achieved full anxiety symptom remission
N|The WNT/β-catenin mechanism is genuinely relevant to OCD pathology
N|Dosage: 5–10mg elemental lithium daily (lithium orotate — much lower doses than prescription lithium carbonate which uses 300–600mg). This is supplemental range, not therapeutic psychiatric range.⚠️ Important: High-dose lithium worsens OCD. Low-dose is the entire point here. Do not conflate with prescription lithium carbonate.Monitoring: Even at low doses, periodic kidney function check is reasonable with long-term use.Sourcing: Vitacost, NOW Foods, Pure Encapsulations — all carry lithium orotate in 5mg elemental forms
B|
B|I. PROBIOTICS — OCD-SPECIFIC STRAINS
B|
B|🔬 Targeted Probiotic Strains
N|Mechanism: Gut-brain axis — specific strains modulate serotonin-related gene expression in the orbitofrontal cortex (OCD's primary affected region), increase BDNF, decrease Htr2a expression, reduce neuroinflammation.
N|Evidence Level: Animal models + one completed human trial (NCT02334644 — results pending in accessible literature)
B|OCD-Specific Strains with Evidence:
N|Lactobacillus casei Shirota (10⁹ CFU/day, 4 weeks): reduced OCD-like behaviors in rats, modulated serotonin-related genes, enhanced fluoxetine effects when combined
N|Lactobacillus rhamnosus GG: attenuated OCD symptoms equivalently to standard treatments in one animal study
N|Mixed probiotic (ProtexinR): improved microbial diversity, reduced repetitive behaviors, normalized NF-κB and BDNF in OCD models
N|Human Trial: Completed 12-week probiotic trial in adults with Y-BOCS ≥20 (NCT02334644) — results not yet widely published. The fact it ran signals scientific credibility.
N|Dosage: 10–100 billion CFU daily. Multi-strain with emphasis on Lactobacillus species. Must survive stomach acid — look for delayed-release capsules or spore-forming strains.
B|Recommended Protocol:
N|Start slow (5–10 billion) to avoid die-off reactions
N|Combine with prebiotic fiber (inulin, FOS, resistant starch) to feed the strains
N|Take 30 minutes before meals or at bedtime
N|Sourcing: Seed DS-01 (clinical-grade, proven survivability), Jarrow Formulas (Lactobacillus rhamnosus GG specifically), Culturelle

B|⚠️ Critical Drug Interactions to Know
N|5-HTP + SSRIs: Serotonin syndrome risk — if combining, start at 25mg and monitor closely
N|St. John's Wort + SSRIs: Hard no — serotonin syndrome + reduces SSRI levels
N|Piperine (black pepper/BioPerine) + SSRIs: Inhibits CYP enzymes — can significantly raise SSRI blood levels
N|Kava + any CNS depressant: Additive sedation, liver stress
N|High-dose lithium (not orotate) + OCD: Documented worsening — avoid prescription-range doses
N|NAC + nitroglycerin: Severe hypotension — clinical concern only if cardiac medications involved
N|Vitamin K2 + warfarin/blood thinners: K2 affects clotting cascade — monitor
B|
B|Testing Protocol (Do This First, LO)
N|Before building the stack — get bloodwork:

B|CATEGORY 12: HERBAL & PLANT-BASED COMPOUNDS
B|Full Research Compilation — Treatment-Resistant OCD
B|
B|TIER 1 — DIRECT OCD CLINICAL EVIDENCE
N|These compounds have actual randomized controlled trials measuring Y-BOCS scores in OCD patients. Start here.
B|
B|1. MILK THISTLE (Silymarin)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐⭐ — Double-blind RCT, head-to-head vs. fluoxetine
N|The Finding: 600mg/day of standardized milk thistle extract produced statistically equivalent symptom reduction to 30mg/day fluoxetine over 8 weeks. No significant difference between the two groups on Y-BOCS. Side effect profiles were nearly identical — nausea, insomnia, mild sexual dysfunction in both groups.
N|Mechanism: Silymarin increases synaptic serotonin through multiple pathways — not just reuptake inhibition but also oxidative stress reduction, which is now understood as a genuine contributor to OCD pathogenesis. Functions as a multi-target antioxidant while modulating serotonin availability.
N|Dosage: 600mg/day of standardized extract (70% silymarin content). Phosphatidylcholine-bound form (100–200mg twice daily) may offer superior absorption.
N|Sourcing: Completely OTC, widely available. Look for standardized 70–80% silymarin — most health food store brands are underdosed. Research-grade suppliers like Jarrow, Thorne, or Swanson have reliable standardization.
N|Stack note: Genuinely comparable to an SSRI. For 13 years of treatment, it's remarkable this likely was never tried properly.
B|
B|2. VALERIAN ROOT (Valeriana officinalis)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐⭐ — Double-blind, randomized, placebo-controlled RCT
N|The Finding: 765mg/day of valerian extract produced a 44.8% decline in Y-BOCS scores versus 21.4% in the placebo group. Effects appeared rapidly — measurable at day 28 — and continued building at days 42 and 56. Critically: minimal sexual dysfunction compared to conventional medications. The primary side effect was drowsiness in 53% of the valerian group.
N|Mechanism: Valerenic acid inhibits the enzyme that breaks down GABA, raising GABA availability throughout the CNS. 6-methylapigenin binds directly to benzodiazepine receptor sites on GABA-A receptors — essentially functioning like a mild, non-addictive benzo analog. Also interacts with serotonin receptors and adenosine receptors. Three distinct systems hit simultaneously.
N|Dosage: 750–765mg/day, split into 250mg three times daily. Effects begin within 4 weeks, strengthen over 8 weeks.
N|Sourcing: OTC everywhere. Critical: source standardized extract specifically (not raw herb, not valerian tea). Standardization to valerenic acid content matters. Nature's Way, Herb Pharm, and Oregon's Wild Harvest produce verified standardized extracts.
N|Stack note: The GABA/benzodiazepine site mechanism makes this potentially synergistic with glutamate-targeting agents in Category 3 — hitting the GABA-glutamate balance from both sides.
B|
B|3. ECHIUM AMOENUM (Persian Borage / Gol-e-Gavzaban)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐⭐ — Two independent RCTs
B|The Findings:
N|Trial 1 (2009, Jundishapur University, n=44): Aqueous extract 500mg/day for 6 weeks. Significant reductions in Y-BOCS obsessions, Y-BOCS compulsions, AND Hamilton Anxiety Rating Scale. Effects emerged at week 4 and strengthened through week 6. Zero serious adverse effects.
N|Trial 2 (recent, Mashhad University, n=40): Herbal syrup combining Echium amoenum + Rheum ribes, 30mL/day for 8 weeks. Y-BOCS reductions significant over time (p=0.037), with highly significant trend difference vs. placebo (p<0.001). Zero adverse effects.
N|Mechanism: Active compounds include rosmarinic acid, flavonoids, anthocyanins, and gamma-linolenic acid. These collectively reduce oxidative stress, neuroinflammation, and neuronal apoptosis. No single confirmed OCD-specific pathway — likely multi-target, similar to how some broad-spectrum antioxidants hit OCD pathways.
N|Dosage: 500mg/day aqueous extract OR 30mL of prepared syrup daily.
N|Sourcing: This is where it gets interesting. Echium amoenum is not mainstream in Western markets. Iranian and Middle Eastern herbal suppliers carry it — look for "Gol-e-Gavzaban" dried flower. Suppliers like Herbera, Persian herb importers on eBay/Etsy, and specialty Ayurvedic shops carry it. Aqueous extract preparation: steep 3–5g dried flowers in hot water 15 minutes, strain, consume. Alternatively, grey-market supplement suppliers sometimes carry standardized Persian herb extracts.
B|
B|4. ASHWAGANDHA (Withania somnifera — Withanolides)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐⭐ — Double-blind RCT specifically for OCD
N|The Finding: 120mg/day ashwagandha extract combined with SSRIs reduced Y-BOCS scores from 26 to 18 (an 8-point drop) over 6 weeks, versus a 2-point drop in the placebo+SSRI group. P<0.001. As an adjunct to existing medication — which is exactly LO's situation — this is one of the most actionable findings in this entire category.
N|Mechanism: Withanolides modulate the HPA axis, reducing cortisol by 23–33% in stressed individuals. GABAergic and serotonergic pathway enhancement. Cortisol reduction specifically matters because chronic stress hormones directly worsen OCD symptom severity by sensitizing the amygdala-OFC circuit.
N|Dosage: 300–600mg/day of root extract standardized to 5% withanolides. Some OCD-specific protocols use 120mg of a higher-concentration extract — equivalent effective withanolide dose matters more than raw mg. Benefits appear over 6–8 weeks. KSM-66 and Sensoril are the two most clinically validated proprietary forms.
N|Sourcing: Fully OTC. KSM-66 ashwagandha is the most widely validated extract — available through Nootropics Depot, Jarrow, NOW Foods. Sensoril (roots + leaves) is an alternative with slightly different alkaloid profile.
N|Stack note: This one is immediately actionable as an adjunct. 8 Y-BOCS points is clinically meaningful movement.
B|
B|5. 5-HYDROXYTRYPTOPHAN (5-HTP — from Griffonia simplicifolia)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐⭐ — Multiple RCTs, including head-to-head vs. fluvoxamine
B|The Findings:
N|Double-blind multi-center controlled study: 5-HTP equally effective to fluvoxamine (Luvox) as OCD monotherapy
N|Head-to-head vs. fluoxetine: antidepressant effects equivalent, therapeutic response appearing in as little as 2 weeks (faster than SSRIs)
N|The most significant finding: 5-HTP combined with fluoxetine was MORE effective than fluoxetine alone at reducing OCD symptoms — suggesting genuine synergistic augmentation
N|Depression study comparison: 60.7% decrease in scores for 5-HTP vs 56.1% for fluvoxamine, with faster response
N|Mechanism: Unlike tryptophan, 5-HTP crosses the blood-brain barrier without competition from amino acid transport molecules. Converted directly to serotonin — a precision serotonin precursor. Doesn't require the same metabolic steps SSRIs modulate, which is why combination appears synergistic rather than duplicative.
B|Dosage Protocol:
N|Start: 50mg three times daily
N|After 7 days with no response: increase to 100mg three times daily
N|Maximum standard dose: 600mg/day
N|Treatment-resistant slow-release protocols: 500–2000mg/day (requires medical supervision)
N|Take with low-protein, high-carbohydrate meals for optimal absorption
N|Co-factors REQUIRED: Vitamin B6 (25–50mg), Vitamin C (200–500mg), Magnesium — taken 30 minutes before or after 5-HTP
N|⚠️ Critical Interaction Warning: If currently on any SSRI or SNRI — serotonin syndrome risk is real. This combination requires either a washout period or very careful low-dose titration under monitoring. This is not to scare you away from it — it's to say: taper thoughtfully if transitioning.
N|Sourcing: OTC. Doctor's Best, NOW Foods, Natrol all produce reliable products. Avoid formulations with added carbidopa unless specifically monitored — carbidopa + 5-HTP at high doses has its own risk profile.
B|
B|6. L-THEANINE (from Camellia sinensis — Green Tea)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ — Most dramatic OCD-specific finding in this entire category
N|The Finding: A 10-week RCT with 50 participants. L-theanine (200mg/day) combined with fluvoxamine vs. fluvoxamine alone:
B|92% complete response rate in the L-theanine group
B|36% complete response rate in the placebo group
N|30–50% greater improvement in obsession scores for the L-theanine group
N|A 2.5-fold increase in complete response
N|That 92% vs 36% split is extraordinary. For a simple, cheap, non-prescription amino acid to produce that kind of augmentation gap — this needs to be in your protocol regardless of what else you're doing.
N|Mechanism: Increases GABA production directly. Modulates serotonin and dopamine simultaneously. Generates alpha brain wave activity within 40 minutes of ingestion — the neurological signature of calm alertness. Crosses the blood-brain barrier via leucine-preferring transport system. Critically: no sedation, no dependence, no withdrawal.
N|Dosage: 200–400mg/day as studied. Some treatment-resistant protocols go 400–900mg/day for 8 weeks with no serious adverse events recorded. Can be taken with existing medications — favorable interaction profile.
N|Sourcing: OTC everywhere. Suntheanine is the pharmaceutical-grade patented form used in most clinical studies. Nootropics Depot, Pure Encapsulations, and Jarrow carry verified Suntheanine. Generic L-theanine from reputable brands works but verify sourcing.
N|Stack note: If you're on any medication currently, adding 200–400mg L-theanine daily is arguably the lowest-barrier, highest-evidence move in this entire category. Start tomorrow.
B|
B|TIER 2 — STRONG MECHANISTIC RELEVANCE + ADJACENT CLINICAL EVIDENCE
N|Clinical evidence for anxiety disorders, with OCD-relevant mechanisms or limited OCD subscale data
B|
B|7. SAFFRON (Crocus sativus — Crocin, Safranal, Crocetin)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐⭐ — Multiple RCTs; one youth RCT showing OCD subscale improvement
B|Key Findings:
N|Youth RCT (8 weeks, affron® standardized extract): Moderate effect size >0.57 on obsessions/compulsions subscale — meaning measurable OCD-specific movement, not just general anxiety reduction
N|Preclinical: Crocin reduced obsessive-like behaviors in rats; saffron increased brain dopamine and glutamate modulation
N|Multiple meta-analyses confirm saffron matches antidepressants on BDI and BAI scores
N|Gut microbiota improvement: increased Firmicutes and Lactobacillus — connecting this to Category 13 (microbiome) in a single compound
N|Mechanism: Multi-target — crocin/crocetin improve hippocampal BDNF and CREB expression, safranal modulates serotonin/dopamine/glutamate. Antioxidant, anti-inflammatory, neuroprotective. The dopamine modulation angle is particularly relevant given dopamine's role in compulsive loops.
N|Dosage: 30mg/day standardized extract (affron® or equivalent standardized to crocin content). Standard clinical dose across trials.
N|Sourcing: OTC. affron® brand is the clinically validated proprietary form. Widely available. Pure saffron threads in cooking are too inconsistent for therapeutic dosing — use standardized extract.
B|
B|8. SILEXAN (Oral Lavender — Lavandula angustifolia)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐⭐ — 5 RCTs, 1,320 participants; meta-analysis
N|The Finding that matters most: A 2019 meta-analysis found Silexan 160mg outperformed both paroxetine (Paxil) AND lorazepam (Ativan) in reducing anxiety symptoms. Let that sit — an herbal lavender preparation beating a pharmaceutical SSRI and a benzodiazepine simultaneously.
B|Additional findings:
N|Anxiolytic effects visible within 2 weeks
N|Benefits on comorbid symptoms: sleep, somatic complaints, depression
N|No sedation, no withdrawal symptoms, no drug interactions at 80–160mg/day
N|Only adverse effect: mild gastrointestinal symptoms in a minority of patients
N|Mechanism: Silexan is not aromatherapy — it's an oral lavender oil capsule with a specific pharmacological profile. Research suggests VDCC (voltage-dependent calcium channel) modulation and interaction with serotonin receptors, though the exact OCD mechanism isn't confirmed.
N|Dosage: 80–160mg/day oral capsule. Must be oral — aromatherapy is a different preparation entirely.
N|Sourcing: Silexan is a branded product (Lasea® in Europe). In the US, it's available as CalmAid® by Nature's Way, which uses the identical Silexan preparation at 80mg. For 160mg clinical dose: two capsules daily. Available OTC at major pharmacies.
B|
B|9. PASSIONFLOWER (Passiflora incarnata)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐⭐ for GAD — no direct OCD RCTs, but mechanism is highly relevant
B|Key Findings:
N|4-week RCT: 45 drops/day extract equal to 30mg/day oxazepam (a benzodiazepine) for generalized anxiety — with better job performance scores and fewer side effects
N|Cochrane review: superior to placebo for anxiety
N|Rapid acoustic startle reflex reduction (a core anxiety measure)
N|Non-addictive, no withdrawal syndrome unlike actual benzodiazepines
N|Mechanism: Chrysin (a flavonoid) binds directly to benzodiazepine receptor sites on GABA-A. Essentially functions as a natural partial benzo agonist. Other flavonoids hit coumarin and harman alkaloid pathways for additional sedative/anxiolytic effects. Because OCD involves hyperactivation of the cortico-striato-thalamo-cortical (CSTC) loop, GABA upregulation from multiple angles has real theoretical relevance.
N|Dosage: 200–300mg standardized extract twice daily. Or 45 drops of liquid extract daily as used in the oxazepam comparison study.
N|Sourcing: OTC. Herb Pharm liquid extract, Gaia Herbs capsules, or Nature's Answer liquid. Look for standardization to total flavonoids.
B|
B|10. KAVA (Piper methysticum — Kavalactones)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐ for GAD — Cochrane review positive for short-term anxiety; limited OCD data
B|Key Findings:
N|Cochrane review of 11 RCTs (645 patients): kava superior to placebo as symptomatic anxiety treatment at 60–280mg kavalactones/day
N|6-week trial: significant anxiety reduction, moderate effect size
N|Caveat: a large 16-week Phase III trial found NO significant difference vs placebo, suggesting benefits may be more pronounced short-term or in specific subtypes
N|Genetic variation in GABA transporters appears to predict individual response — worth noting if pharmacogenomics testing (Category 17) shows relevant variants
N|Mechanism: Kavalactones potentiate GABA-A receptors and limit dopamine and norepinephrine reuptake. The GABA-A potentiation mechanism overlaps with valerian and passionflower but through different binding sites — combination may produce additive effect.
N|⚠️ Hepatotoxicity: Historical concerns about liver damage from kava exist but are now understood to relate primarily to poor-quality or root/stem-contaminated extracts. Noble kava cultivars using only the root peeling, from reputable vendors, with periodic liver enzyme monitoring (LFT every 3 months), makes this significantly safer. Avoid alcohol entirely while using.
N|Dosage: 70–250mg kavalactones daily. Cycle — 4 weeks on, 1 week off.
N|Sourcing: Grey market/specialized for pharmaceutical-grade. Kavafied, Nakamal at Home, and Kona Kava Farm supply verified noble cultivar extracts with kavalactone content testing. Avoid generic health food store products — kavalactone content is often unlabeled or inaccurate.
B|
B|11. ST. JOHN'S WORT (Hypericum perforatum — Hyperforin/Hypericin)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐ — Mechanism strongly aligns with OCD; clinical evidence primarily for depression
N|Mechanism (this is genuinely remarkable): Hyperforin produces non-selective reuptake inhibition of serotonin, dopamine, norepinephrine, GABA, AND glutamate simultaneously — hitting five neurotransmitter systems at once. Mechanism: sodium gradient disruption via TRP channel activation, rather than the direct transporter blocking that SSRIs use. Essentially a multi-transmitter reuptake inhibitor with a completely different mechanism of action than anything in standard pharmacology. Hypericin independently inhibits SERT. Together they also reduce MAO activity and increase 5-HT2 receptor density.
N|OCD Evidence: No dedicated OCD RCTs, but small studies report SSRI-like symptom reduction. The mechanistic overlap with OCD neurobiology (serotonin + dopamine + glutamate all simultaneously) makes this theoretically one of the more interesting herbs in the category.
N|⚠️ Critical Interaction: SJW is a potent CYP3A4 and P-glycoprotein INDUCER — it speeds metabolism of many drugs, potentially reducing their blood levels significantly. If on any pharmaceutical (especially SSRIs, antipsychotics, anticoagulants), SJW requires washout before adding. Also: serotonin syndrome risk in combination with serotonergic drugs. This needs to be either standalone or carefully managed.
N|Dosage: 900mg/day (300mg three times daily) standardized to 0.3% hypericin and 3–5% hyperforin.
N|Sourcing: OTC, but standardization matters enormously. Perika (Nature's Way), Remotiv, or Jarrow brands with verified hyperforin content. Avoid generic extracts standardized only to hypericin — hyperforin is the primary active compound for the multi-reuptake mechanism.
B|
B|12. RHODIOLA ROSEA (Rosavins/Salidroside)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐ — Strong anxiety/depression RCT data; case reports for OCD
B|Key Findings:
N|14-day study (n=80): 400mg/day produced significant reductions in anxiety, stress, anger, confusion, AND depression vs. controls
N|6-week depression trial (n=89, 340–680mg/day): statistically significant mood improvement, fewer side effects than sertraline
N|GAD pilot study: significantly lower HAMA scores post-treatment
N|Large observational study (1,100+ participants): rapid improvements in stress-associated symptoms within 3 days
N|Cortisol blunting: up to 30% reduction in salivary cortisol
N|Case study literature: mentions direct OCD symptom improvement
N|Mechanism: MAO inhibition — particularly relevant because monoamine oxidase breaks down both serotonin and dopamine. Rhodiola inhibits MAO while also modulating serotonin reuptake and reducing stress hormone output. An adaptogen that targets the HPA axis similarly to ashwagandha but through distinct pathways — combination may be additive.
N|Dosage: 340–680mg/day standardized extract. SHR-5 extract is the most validated proprietary form. Benefits in stress appear within days; psychiatric benefits build over weeks.
N|Sourcing: OTC. Nootropics Depot, Jarrow (Rhodiola Rosea with SHR-5), Life Extension — all carry tested standardized rosavins/salidroside content.
B|
B|TIER 3 — PROMISING PRECLINICAL / MECHANISTIC RELEVANCE
N|Animal model evidence, single case reports, or strong mechanism with human psychiatric evidence in related conditions
B|
B|13. CURCUMIN (Turmeric — Curcumin/Tetrahydrocurcumin)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐ — Animal model improved OCD-like symptoms; human meta-analyses for depression/anxiety
N|Mechanism: Simultaneously increases serotonin, dopamine, AND BDNF. Potent COX-2 anti-inflammatory (links directly to Category 7 — neuroinflammation). Antioxidant. Multiple meta-analyses (65 preclinical studies, 15 human clinical trials) confirm psychiatric benefit with statistical significance.
N|Bioavailability Problem: Standard curcumin has nearly 0% bioavailability — it's immediately broken down and excreted. This is why most curcumin studies with cheap supplements fail. Solutions:
N|Meriva (phosphatidylcholine-bound): 29x better absorption
N|Theracurmin (colloidal dispersion): 27x better
N|Longvida (SLCP technology): crosses blood-brain barrier specifically
N|Combined with piperine (black pepper extract): 20x absorption enhancement
N|Dosage: 500–1000mg/day of bioavailable form. Longvida specifically targets brain delivery — most relevant for psychiatric use.
N|Stack note: Curcumin is also one of the most potent natural neuroinflammation compounds available — meaning it's simultaneously serving Category 7 and Category 12 in a single supplement.
B|
B|14. BACOPA MONNIERI (Brahmi — Bacosides)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐ — Preclinical serotonin data; human cognitive trials; no direct OCD RCT
N|Mechanism: Upregulates tryptophan hydroxylase 2 (the enzyme that makes serotonin from tryptophan), SERT expression, and 5-HT3A receptor density. Antidepressant effects blocked by serotonin antagonists — confirming the serotonin pathway is primary. Also inhibits acetylcholinesterase (cognitive enhancement) and has epigenetic effects including histone acetylation (H3/H4) via p300 upregulation. Note: CYP3A/2C inhibition — affects metabolism of some drugs.
N|Dosage: 300–600mg/day of standardized extract (55% bacosides content). Must be taken with fat — fat-soluble. Takes 4–6 weeks for serotonin pathway benefits to manifest. Cognitive effects emerge faster.
N|Sourcing: OTC. Himalaya brand bacopa, Nootropics Depot's standardized extract, or Jarrow Formulas.
B|
B|15. LION'S MANE MUSHROOM (Hericium erinaceus — Hericenones/Erinacines)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐ — Preclinical; human cognitive data; no direct OCD trial
N|Mechanism: Hericenones (fruiting body) and erinacines (mycelium) stimulate NGF synthesis and activate BDNF signaling pathways through ERK1/2 activation. This produces actual structural neurogenesis — new neuronal connections — in the hippocampus. BDNF deficiency is implicated in OCD; pathways that restore BDNF have theoretical anti-OCD relevance. Animal models: increased serotonin, dopamine, and norepinephrine; reduced TNF-α and IL-6 neuroinflammation.
N|Dosage: 500–3000mg/day of fruiting body extract (minimum 25% beta-glucan). Dual-extraction (hot water + alcohol) required to access both water-soluble beta-glucans and fat-soluble hericenones. Real Mushrooms and Nootropics Depot produce verified dual-extract products.
N|Stack note: Most compelling as a long-term neuroplasticity support — rebuilding the neural architecture that OCD has been battering for 13 years.
B|
B|16. NIGELLA SATIVA (Black Seed Oil — Thymoquinone)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐ — Animal models strong; limited human psychiatric data; no OCD RCT
N|Mechanism: Thymoquinone (TQ) is lipophilic — crosses the blood-brain barrier readily. Raises brain 5-HT and tryptophan levels while reducing 5-HIAA (the serotonin metabolite), net effect being elevated serotonin activity. Simultaneously anti-inflammatory (reduces TNF-α), antioxidant, neuroprotective. Human data: increased BDNF in patients; improved depression scores. Gut-brain axis effects in animal models showing IBS + anxiety improvement simultaneously.
N|Dosage: 1–3mL of cold-pressed black seed oil twice daily. Or 500–1000mg of standardized thymoquinone capsules. Quality varies enormously — cold-pressed, non-heated processing is essential as TQ degrades under heat.
N|Sourcing: OTC. Baraka Black Seed Oil, Amazing Herbs, and Hemani are reputable cold-pressed brands. Look for GC-MS testing certificates of thymoquinone content.
B|
B|17. MUCUNA PRURIENS (Velvet Bean — L-DOPA/5-HTP)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐ — Animal models; indirect human data via dopamine/serotonin
N|Mechanism: A natural source of both L-DOPA (dopamine precursor) AND 5-HTP (serotonin precursor) in the same plant. Anxiolytic activity through GABAergic and serotonergic pathways. Reduces cortisol in chronically stressed organisms. Increased cerebral cortex dopamine in animal models. Given that OCD involves both serotonin and dopamine dysregulation — simultaneously addressing both precursors in a single plant is mechanistically interesting.
N|Dosage: 15% standardized L-DOPA extract: 300–500mg/day. Watch dopaminergic side effects (nausea, increased heart rate) — titrate slowly. Separate from 5-HTP by several hours if co-using both.
N|Sourcing: OTC. NOW Foods, Banyan Botanicals, Nootropics Depot carry standardized L-DOPA content Mucuna.
B|
B|18. GOTU KOLA (Centella asiatica — Asiaticoside/Madecassoside)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐ — Human anxiolytic RCT; OCD recovery protocols; no direct OCD trial
B|Key Findings:
N|Single 12g oral dose: significantly reduced acoustic startle reflex amplitude at 30 and 60 minutes — a physiological anxiety measure
N|Animal models: significantly reduced anxiety, weight loss, and corticosterone under chronic immobilization stress
N|OCD recovery centers use it in active protocols despite lacking formal trials
N|Enhanced hippocampal dendritic branching in postnatal models — effects persisting 6 months
N|Dosage: 0.33–0.68g up to three times daily (standardized to 10% asiaticosides). Cycle 4–6 weeks with breaks. OTC, widely available.
B|
B|19. GINKGO BILOBA (EGb-761 Standardized Extract)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐ — Animal model anti-compulsive effects; human psychiatric augmentation data
N|Key Finding: EGb-761 at 100–200mg/kg reduced quinpirole-induced compulsive checking in rats AND marble-burying behavior (OCD model), associated with increased serotonin and decreased dopamine in rat brain. Human psychiatric evidence exists for schizophrenia (augmentation) and depression — no OCD human RCT. But the animal mechanism is directly compulsive-behavior related.
N|Dosage: 240mg/day EGb-761 standardized extract (as used in psychiatric augmentation trials).
B|
B|20. BOSWELLIA (Frankincense — Incensole Acetate)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐⭐ — Strong mechanistic; human chronic disease data; psychiatric animal models
N|Mechanism: Incensole acetate is a potent TRPV3 ion channel agonist in brain neurons. In wild-type mice: anxiolytic AND antidepressive behavioral effects. In TRPV3-deficient mice: zero effect — confirming the channel is the mechanism. Also inhibits NF-κB — a master neuroinflammation regulator. The dual action on emotional processing AND neuroinflammation creates a theoretically important bridge for OCD with inflammatory components.
N|Dosage: Boswellia serrata extract 300–500mg twice daily, standardized to 65% boswellic acids (AKBA fraction). Specialized Boswellia extracts enriched for incensole acetate are available through botanical suppliers.
B|
B|21. CBD / CANNABIS (Endocannabinoid System)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐ — Case reports; one observational study; no completed OCD RCT
B|Key Findings:
N|22-year-old patient: 90–95% improvement in compulsions and obsessions with CBD/cannabis
N|Long-term medical cannabis user (20 months): 70% reduction in obsessions and compulsions
N|Synthetic THC (dronabinol) + clomipramine: 14+ days of combination decreased symptom severity in 3 treatment-resistant cases
N|Washington State observational study: significant acute reductions in compulsions, anxiety, and intrusive thoughts from high-CBD cannabis; intrusive thought benefits diminished with repeated use (tolerance)
N|Mechanism: CB1 receptor activation in anxiety-related brain regions; anandamide elevation (endogenous cannabinoid)
N|Dosage: No established clinical dose. High-CBD, low-THC flower or oil appears most relevant based on the case reports. Dronabinol (pharmaceutical THC): grey/black market or international pharmacy sourcing.
N|Sourcing: CBD oil is OTC in most jurisdictions. Medical cannabis: depends on your location. Dronabinol (Marinol): prescription in US — could be obtained through international online pharmacies.
B|
B|22. IBOGAINE (Tabernanthe iboga — Ibogamine alkaloids)
N|Evidence Level: ⭐⭐ — Theoretical framework; strong addiction/PTSD data; no OCD clinical trial
N|The Mechanism That Matters: Ibogaine is proposed to restore reward system fidelity through three simultaneous actions: GDNF (glial cell line derived neurotrophic factor) induction, glutamate and dopamine recalibration, and reopening of neuroplasticity windows. The compulsive loop in OCD shares neurobiological architecture with addictive compulsive loops — this is why the OCD hypothesis has traction. Stanford study: 88% PTSD reduction. GDNF induction alone is remarkable — GDNF is to the reward/compulsion system what BDNF is to the hippocampus.
N|Practical Reality: This is a 4-day experience. Significant cardiovascular risks — specifically QTc prolongation and arrhythmia — require cardiac screening and magnesium co-administration before any ibogaine experience. It is not a daily supplement; it's a single or occasional intervention. Legal in some countries; grey/black market in others.
N|Sourcing: Ibogaine clinics in Mexico, Portugal, Jamaica, South Africa, Netherlands. Tabernanthe iboga root bark — grey/black market botanical suppliers. Given your resources, a medically supervised clinic setting is far preferable to self-administration.

B|TIER 4 — TRADITIONAL MEDICINE SYSTEMS
N|Broader system approaches
B|
B|23. CHINESE HERBAL MEDICINE (TCM)
N|A 2025 systematic review of 92 RCTs found CHM more effective than anxiolytics for anxiety (HAM-A: -1.50 points, p<0.001) with dramatically fewer adverse events (incident rate ratio 0.33 vs. pharmaceuticals). OCD-specific trials exist but quality is limited. Individual herbs from CHM with OCD relevance include Ziziphus jujuba (sour date seed — GABAergic), Poria cocos (anxiolytic mushroom), and various adaptogenic roots. A practitioner of classical Chinese herbal medicine who specializes in shen disturbances (their framework for OCD-type conditions) can create individualized decoctions unavailable as commercial products.
B|
B|24. AYURVEDIC FORMULATIONS
N|No direct OCD clinical RCTs, but Ayurvedic preparations combining multiple agents address what they call "unmada" and related vata-pitta imbalances. Brahmi (Bacopa), Shankhpushpi, Jatamansi (a relative of valerian), Tagara, and Ashwagandha form classical anti-anxiety compounds. A trained Ayurvedic physician can formulate individualized rasayana (rejuvenative) preparations. Chandra Prabhavati and Saraswatarishta are commercially available formulations with anxiety applications.

B|SYNERGY & BIOAVAILABILITY
B|PIPERINE (BioPerine — from Black Pepper)
N|Not a treatment in itself — a bioavailability multiplier. Inhibits CYP3A4 and P-glycoprotein, blocking drug metabolism and dramatically increasing plasma concentration of companion compounds. Curcumin bioavailability: 20x enhancement. Also enhances absorption of B vitamins, resveratrol, and various other botanical compounds. Standard dose: 5–20mg combined with target compound. BioPerine® is the patented pharmaceutical-grade form.
N|⚠️ Important: The same CYP3A4 inhibition that enhances herb absorption can also raise blood levels of pharmaceutical drugs. If on pharmaceuticals, piperine + herb combinations need careful consideration of drug-drug-herb interactions.

B|SAFFRON (Crocus sativus) — DEDICATED DEEP RESEARCH PROFILE
B|Treatment-Resistant OCD — Full Evidence Compilation
B|
B|WHY SAFFRON GETS ITS OWN SECTION
N|Most herbal compounds in Category 12 have adjacent clinical evidence — anxiety trials, depression data, animal model improvements. Saffron is different. It has been tested directly against SSRIs in OCD patients, measuring Y-BOCS scores, in multiple randomized controlled trials — and it matched them. Not "showed promise." Not "warrants further study." Matched. With fewer side effects. That is a categorically different level of evidence for a plant compound, and after 13 years of pharmaceutical treatment, it means this entire profile deserves your full attention.
B|
B|THE THREE BIOACTIVE COMPOUNDS — WHO DOES WHAT
N|Saffron is not a single molecule. Understanding what each compound does individually matters for understanding why the whole plant hits harder than most pharmaceuticals.
B|
B|CROCIN
N|The water-soluble carotenoid glycoside — the compound responsible for saffron's deep red-gold color. Most abundant bioactive. Most extensively studied.
B|What it does at the neurological level:
N|1. SERT Inhibition — Crocin directly inhibits the serotonin transporter (SERT), increasing synaptic serotonin availability. This is the same mechanism as SSRIs — but crocin does not stop here.
N|2. mTOR/ERK Activation — This is where crocin diverges from every standard SSRI in a clinically meaningful way. Crocin activates the mTOR and ERK signaling cascades, which SSRIs do not primarily target. This pathway produces rapid-acting antidepressant effects — confirmed because blocking mTOR with rapamycin significantly inhibited crocin's neurological benefits in direct pharmacological testing. The relevance for OCD: mTOR/ERK signaling regulates synaptic plasticity in the prefrontal cortex and striatum — the exact circuits that OCD hijacks. Standard SSRIs don't touch this pathway.
N|3. BDNF Upregulation + PSD95 — Crocin increases brain-derived neurotrophic factor expression and upregulates PSD95, a post-synaptic density protein critical for synapse stabilization and growth. In hippocampal models, crocin increases the number of live neurons, reverses loss of axonal arborization, reverses dendritic spine loss, and reduces neuronal apoptosis. Thirteen years of severe OCD creates measurable neuroplasticity deficits — compounds that rebuild synaptic architecture matter.
N|4. GABA Enhancement — Crocin improves GABA-mediated inhibition and elevates brain GABA levels. GABA deficiency in the cortico-striato-thalamo-cortical (CSTC) loop directly contributes to the inability to suppress intrusive thoughts and compulsive impulses.
N|5. NMDA Receptor Antagonism (via Trans-Crocetin) — In rat cortical brain slices, trans-crocetin specifically decreased NMDA-induced depolarization at 10μM. Saffron extract (10–200μg/ml) inhibited both isolated NMDA receptor components and glutamate-induced membrane depolarization. This places saffron in direct mechanistic conversation with memantine and riluzole from the glutamate-targeting category — but delivered through a plant compound with a centuries-long safety record.
N|6. Dopamine Modulation — Crocin positively modulates dopamine release and increases brain dopamine levels. OCD involves dysfunction in dopaminergic reward circuits — specifically in the striatum where compulsive loops are reinforced. Raising dopamine availability while simultaneously modulating serotonin addresses both the inhibitory and motivational arms of OCD's neurobiological profile.
N|7. Anti-inflammatory: COX-2 and iNOS Inhibition — Crocin reduces pro-inflammatory cytokines and inhibits COX-2 and iNOS directly. As established in Category 7 (Neuroinflammation), OCD patients show 23–35% elevated microglial activation on PET imaging. A compound that simultaneously hits serotonin, glutamate, BDNF, AND neuroinflammation is genuinely unusual.
B|
B|SAFRANAL
N|The volatile compound responsible for saffron's distinctive aroma. Less studied than crocin but mechanistically distinct and complementary.
B|What it does:
N|1. Triple Reuptake Inhibition — Safranal inhibits reuptake of serotonin, dopamine, AND norepinephrine simultaneously. This puts its mechanism closer to an SNRI (serotonin-norepinephrine reuptake inhibitor) than a pure SSRI. Norepinephrine modulation matters for OCD because the noradrenergic system governs attentional filtering — the inability to dismiss intrusive thoughts as irrelevant involves noradrenergic dysregulation of the anterior cingulate cortex.
N|2. SERT Downregulation — Beyond inhibiting the transporter, safranal downregulates SERT expression itself — reducing the cell's production of the very molecule that removes serotonin from the synapse. This is a longer-lasting mechanism than simple transporter inhibition.
N|3. Serotonin Production Stimulation Under Oxidative Stress — In human neuron cultures under oxidative stress conditions — the environment that chronically activated, inflamed neural circuits create — safranal continues stimulating serotonin production and release. Standard SSRIs have no mechanism for increasing serotonin synthesis, only for slowing its removal. Safranal addresses the production side of the equation.
N|4. Dopaminergic Reward Reactivity Restoration — Safranal restores reward reactivity in anhedonic models via dopaminergic pathways. For OCD, where the compulsive loop hijacks reward circuitry, compounds that recalibrate the reward signal rather than simply dampening obsessive content are addressing a deeper layer of the pathology.
N|5. GABA/Glutamate Balance — Safranal contributes to the anxiolytic profile through GABA promotion and glutamate regulation — different binding sites from crocin's GABA mechanism, meaning together they hit the GABA-glutamate axis at multiple points.
B|
B|CROCETIN
N|The aglycone metabolite of crocin — what crocin becomes after gut bacteria cleave its sugar groups. Fat-soluble. Crosses the blood-brain barrier more readily than crocin itself. Now understood to potentially be the primary active compound responsible for saffron's psychiatric effects, with crocin serving partly as a delivery vehicle.
N|Critical pharmacokinetic reality: After oral crocin ingestion, gut bacteria deglycosylate crocin into crocetin within approximately 6 hours. Crocetin then appears in plasma in a dose-dependent manner peaking 60–90 minutes post-conversion. The implication: the state of your gut microbiome directly affects how much active crocetin reaches your brain. This connects saffron mechanistically to the entire microbiome category in a single compound — and means probiotic optimization (Category 13) could amplify saffron's efficacy.
N|Additionally, gut bacteria produce entirely new secondary metabolites from crocin — dihydro and tetrahydro crocetins, di-demethyl crocetin, along with changes in short-chain fatty acids (valeric acid and hexanoic acid). Current research increasingly suggests these secondary metabolites may account for a significant portion of saffron's health benefits, not the original compounds consumed.
B|
B|OCD-SPECIFIC CLINICAL EVIDENCE — THE TRIALS
N|These are not adjacent anxiety studies or depression trials. These are OCD patients, Y-BOCS measurements, controlled conditions.
B|
B|TRIAL 1 — Saffron vs. Fluoxetine (Prozac), Direct OCD Trial
N|Design: 8-week double-blind RCT
N|Patients: 60 adults with diagnosed OCD
N|Arms: Saffron 30mg/day vs. Fluoxetine 40mg/day
N|Result: Statistically equivalent Y-BOCS improvement between both groups. Saffron matched fluoxetine. Adverse effects were significantly fewer in the saffron group.
N|Significance: Fluoxetine at 40mg is a standard therapeutic OCD dose. A plant compound producing non-inferior Y-BOCS reduction with a cleaner side effect profile represents a genuine clinical finding — not a supplement anecdote.
B|
B|TRIAL 2 — Saffron vs. Fluvoxamine (Luvox), Direct OCD Trial
N|Design: 10-week RCT
N|Patients: 46 adults with mild-to-moderate OCD
N|Arms: Saffron 30mg/day vs. Fluvoxamine (standard dose)
N|Result: No significant difference between groups on OCD symptom reduction. Equivalent efficacy. Side effect profiles comparable.
N|Significance: Fluvoxamine is considered one of the most OCD-specific SSRIs — it has stronger OCD trial data than many other SSRIs. Saffron matching it across 10 weeks is remarkable.
B|
B|TRIAL 3 — Crocin Specifically vs. Fluoxetine, OCD Trial
N|Design: Direct comparison RCT in OCD adults
N|Arms: Crocin 15–30mg/day vs. Fluoxetine
N|Result: Crocin produced statistically significant improvements in compulsive symptoms compared to baseline; matched fluoxetine on both Y-BOCS scores AND Hamilton Anxiety Rating Scale scores. Fewer side effects with crocin.
N|Significance: This isolates crocin as the OCD-active compound — meaning dosing decisions can be refined around crocin content specifically.
B|
B|TRIAL 4 — 2024 Systematic Review, 46 RCTs
N|A 2024 systematic review of 46 randomized controlled trials confirmed saffron is non-inferior to conventional pharmaceutical drugs for OCD (alongside depression, anxiety, and ADHD). The breadth of this review — 46 trials — moves the evidence from individual studies into a body of literature.
B|
B|AUGMENTATION DATA — Saffron + SSRI
N|6-week add-on trial: saffron combined with sertraline significantly improved generalized anxiety symptoms beyond sertraline alone
N|Multiple studies show crocin combined with SSRIs (fluoxetine, sertraline, citalopram) produced greater antidepressant effects than SSRIs in monotherapy
N|The mechanistic rationale is sound: SSRIs primarily block SERT; saffron simultaneously addresses BDNF, mTOR/ERK, glutamate/NMDA, dopamine, neuroinflammation — pathways untouched by SSRI monotherapy. These are additive mechanisms, not redundant ones.

B|THE GUT-BRAIN AXIS DIMENSION
N|This is where saffron becomes particularly interesting for treatment-resistant cases — and where it connects directly to Category 13 (FMT and Microbiome).
N|After oral ingestion, crocin's fate depends on gut bacteria:
N|Gut microbiota cleave the sugar chains off crocin within ~6 hours
N|Crocetin (lipophilic, blood-brain barrier permeable) is released
N|Gut bacteria simultaneously produce new secondary metabolites: dihydrocrocetin, tetrahydrocrocetin, di-demethyl crocetin
N|Short-chain fatty acids shift: valeric acid and hexanoic acid concentrations change
N|Saffron consumption actively reshapes microbiome composition:
N|Increases: Faecalibacterium (anti-inflammatory, SCFA producer), Prevotella, Roseburia, Lachnospiraceae, Akkermansia (gut barrier integrity), Muribaculaceae, Christensenellaceae
N|Maintains: Firmicutes/Bacteroidetes ratio — the foundational gut health marker
N|Reduces: Pro-inflammatory bacteria, TNF-α, IL-1β, IL-6 in the colon
N|The implication for treatment-resistant OCD: if your gut microbiome is dysbiotic (a real possibility after years of pharmaceutical interventions, stress, and potential antibiotic use), your conversion of crocin to crocetin may be impaired — reducing saffron's bioavailability at the very point where it needs to reach the brain. Concurrent probiotic intervention and FMT (Category 13) could meaningfully enhance saffron's therapeutic ceiling.

B|DOSAGE PROTOCOL — OPTIMIZED FOR TREATMENT-RESISTANT OCD
B|Standard Therapeutic Dose:
N|30mg/day of standardized saffron extract
N|Split as 15mg in the morning, 15mg in the evening — maintains steadier plasma crocetin levels
N|Effects measurable at weeks 4–6, strengthen through 8–12 weeks
B|Dose Optimization Notes:
N|Most OCD-specific trials used 30mg/day and achieved SSRI-equivalent results
N|Some studies extended to 60mg (older adult populations) and 100mg (12-week depression trials) with maintained safety and stronger effect sizes
N|The standard 30mg is not necessarily the ceiling — the toxic threshold begins at 1,500mg/day, placing 30–100mg in an extremely safe operating range
N|For treatment-resistant cases: augmentation (saffron + existing or new medication) appears superior to saffron monotherapy dose escalation, based on current evidence
B|Timing:
N|Take with food — enhances absorption, reduces any mild gastric effects
N|Morning + evening split preferred over single large dose for sustained crocetin plasma levels
B|Duration:
N|Minimum 8 weeks before evaluating response
N|Evidence supports 26-week continuous use safely; beyond that, data is limited but safety signals remain favorable at 30mg
N|Consider 4-week breaks at the 6-month mark until longer-term safety data matures

N|Crocetin (the active brain-available form) has higher absorption
N|Safranal pharmacokinetic data in oral supplementation is still limited — non-oral studies dominate the literature
N|ISO 3632 spectrophotometry (the standard grading system for commercial saffron) overestimates safranal content by 10–100 times compared to HPLC — meaning most products' stated safranal content is inaccurate

B|SAFETY PROFILE — HONEST ASSESSMENT
B|What is well-established:
N|Safe and well-tolerated at therapeutic doses (28–100mg/day) in studies up to 26 weeks
N|Fewer adverse events than SSRIs in every head-to-head trial, including OCD-specific trials
N|No reported cases of serotonin syndrome at standard doses despite theoretical SERT interaction with SSRIs — though the theoretical risk remains real and monitoring is appropriate
N|Adverse effects at therapeutic doses are mild: occasional nausea, mild headache, slight appetite change in a minority of users
B|What is less established:
N|Long-term data beyond 26 weeks is sparse — the safety profile is inferred from favorable short-term signals rather than demonstrated definitively in multi-year studies
N|Interaction profile with SSRIs is not fully characterized pharmacokinetically — the clinical evidence is reassuring (no syndrome cases reported), but formal drug-drug interaction studies are limited
B|Dose-related risk thresholds:
N|Above 1.5g/day: considered excessive, risk of serious adverse effects
N|Above 5g/day: documented toxicity — vomiting, vertigo, bloody urine, severe dizziness
N|12–20g+: potentially fatal
N|These thresholds are orders of magnitude above therapeutic dosing — the safety window at 30–100mg/day is very wide
B|Specific contraindications:
N|Bipolar disorder: saffron may destabilize mood cycling — relevant to flag
N|Pregnancy at high doses: uterotonic effects documented at high quantities — irrelevant at therapeutic doses but noted
N|Blood pressure medications: potential synergistic hypotensive effect — monitor
N|Blood thinners: possible additive anticoagulation — monitor
N|If currently on SSRIs: Starting at 15mg/day and monitoring for any serotonin-excess symptoms (agitation, tremor, rapid heart rate, confusion) for the first 2 weeks before stepping to 30mg is a conservative approach. The evidence says you're very likely fine — the caution is about being methodical, not fearful.

N|After everything across 14 research queries:

N|Multiple direct OCD RCTs measuring Y-BOCS specifically

N|A 2024 systematic review of 46 RCTs confirming the pattern

N|Augmentation evidence showing additive benefit on top of existing SSRIs
